I visited Miracle Ear 6 months ago when my wife suggested we have our hearing tested.  (I already knew that my hearing was poor since birth).

Spencer, at the Cupertino office, is very professional and very good at making sure a customers needs are met.  He is a real pleasure to work with.

On my first visit, I was quite amazed at the testing and hearing aid programming process.  Being an electrical engineer familiar with frequency response measurements during school, it was fascinating seeing the programmed response curve being overlaid on the measurement data.  What is truly amazing is how natural the sound is.  I almost forget that I am wearing them sometimes.<//Text>

< text>
Before getting into the review itself, I should say I am very pleased with every aspect of Miracle Ear the company and the product, as well as my experience with the staff at the office -- they made the process simple, smooth, and easy, and the hearing aids I got are the best I've ever had. I'm 64 and now after all these years I feel I'm hearing better than when I was a teenager.

No product is perfect, of course; however  these hearing aids are so much better than the product I bought 8 years ago, it's amazing -- they're really opening up new opportunities for having a better social life.

I bought a top-line pair of hearing aids from the Miracle Ear office in Cupertino, CA. Before choosing this company I did a *lot* of research, and I called several local providers to get an appointment. Miracle Ear was the first and only one I went to, because they convinced me in one session that their hearing aid was the right one for me.

I was helped by Aaron Gabrielson. Aaron started by finding out about my needs, and did a free hearing test right there on the spot as part of the first visit. The results were that I was suffering from significant hearing loss, and these results matched the profile I obtained from my audiologist in the Palo Alto Medical Foundation.

Aaron answered all my questions and was extremely professional, knowledgeable, and also very enjoyable to work with. I feel that he and Rachel really care about my needs and work hard to produce exceptional results for me. Over the follow-up visits (see below) I got to know them better and I really like them -- exceptional professionals and warm people.

The great thing about Miracle Ear is that they do not just sell you hearing aids and forget about you. Instead, they pretty much require you to come in for a series of follow up visits that start once you get your hearing aids, and during these visits Aaron fine-tuned the hearing aids to better match what my hearing loss requires. This is a process whereby your ears and brain get "retrained" to process all the new information that your ears hear. Aaron was always polite, respectful and very helpful.

As with everything, there are some negatives as well. The most significant I'll mention is the price. The hearing aids I bought are the most expensive ones I've ever purchased. Very expensive. But once you consider everything I got, the value is exceptional -- I am now hearing much better than I've ever had, since being a teenager, the time my hearing loss started. The technology is really cutting edge and produces exceptional amplification of what you WANT to hear while suppressing background noises. And the follow-up program and periodic tuning, plus the gradual approach taken, is based on recognizing that people need some adjustment time, and most cannot tolerate the huge jump in what they hear all at once. I believe this approach results in much better results.

I'll close by saying that I've been talking the ears off everyone who will listen (and some people that did not want to listen) about getting hearing aids and recommending the Cupertino office. Two thumbs up!</text>

1556170331449</date>
<pics>None</pics><Review>TL,DR: Avoid this place if you are a trucker and like to make money.  Staff is okay, place seems severely disorganized.

I normally don't go around leaving negative reviews, but this is one of the most disorganized shipping facilities I've been to. The staff were friendly enough, so it was more of a left hand didn't know what the right hand was doing kind of thing .

I arrived at about 1230 for my 1300 appointment and checked in. Was told I'd have a little wait, so no big deal at first. I also noticed everytime I came in the dock was a cluster of pallets.  Maybe they had some sort of system to it, but I couldn't tell.

I checked back 2 hours later and they seemed to have "misplaced" my load papers with my name/number/info on it .So, after about 5 minutes they were able to finally print out a new sheet and I filled that out.  I was told I still had a 5-6 hour wait. Starting to get rediculous, but I know things get backed up some times .

Fast forward to about 0100 hours (12 hours after having checked in).  The night crew is no on and I check to see what's going on.  Lo and behold, they can't find my paperwork anywhere. So, after 5 more minutes of the guy messing with the computer, we fill out yet another sheet with the same info. This time I'm told there are 7 trucks ahead of me. When I ask how that's so since I've been waiting for so long (and have been watching trucks that arrived way after me get loaded), I'm met with the response of "I wasn't here when you checked in."  Good job answering my question.

So the next morning, after sitting for 20+ hours at this point, I'm pulled off the load and sent elsewhere. As a courtesy, I go in to let the office know I'm leaving.  I got to wait another 5 minutes while they tried to (and finally did) find my paperwork .

Everytime I went in, it seemed a vast majority of the paperwork was in random spots throughout the office.  This place seriously needs to rethink what they are doing.  Had I stayed there, I would've maybe had one driving shift (11 hours max) to drive over 1,000 miles for the delivery.< /Review>< response>
None</response>

<Text>This place is a hidden Gem in the Torrance Area! We always get out of our workouts late and look for places open later on a Friday night.

Not only do they have convenient hours, but heir food is so tasty, fresh and super affordable!!

I love their chicken Pho bowl and their Shrimp tempura appetizer plate!! Their food is wholesome, light and their cooking has a home real home made feel and taste too.

Did I mention they have smoothies too!!

Try their watermelon juice! Refreshing and sweet!!

I wish their chairs and tables were not wobbly, that is the only complaint I have.

2nd the staff was amazing and always are. I have returned on three occasions and each time I walk out in a more pleasant mood simply because the staff knows how to be nice, friendly and courteous.

3rd the speediness of the whole process. I was in and out in less than 30 minutes.

There are many benefits to choosing this as your medical marijuana doctor, my favorite has to be the simple and easy 24/7 verification process. Makes life so much more simple when registering at a dispensary for the first time. I will continue to go here for years to come.</Text>

< text>
We went to the restaurant about 5:45 pm for dinner. We were told that a table would be available in 20-25 minutes. We sat for at least 45 minutes before being seated. The problem was that the restaurant had a 4-6 pm happy hour with discounted drinks and appetizers. About half the tables were occupied, by people who came for that happy hour special continued to stay at their tables, some ordering more wine and not mindful that the happy hour had ended.
We asked the waitstaff about this and they said that they would not inform patrons that happy hour had ended and that they could either order from the full dinner menu or leave to make room for dinner patrons.
With only 6-8 small tables this would have been a more efficient way of handling the patrons.
Those of us wanting to have a full dining experience were compromised by a few ‚Äúhangers on‚Äù happy hour drinkers and the waitstaff did nothing to alleviate the problem. This would not have been a problem with endless seating options but was a gross mismanagement of a very small venue.
Neil & Karen, Carmel residents.</text>

< review>
Lisa and I had the opportunity to visit this cozy modern restaurant on a recent visit. The decor is elegant and also exudes a romantic ambiance. The restaurant features a bar that can accommodate walk-in guests, and has a well-selected wine list that can be easily paired with many of the selections on the menu. We were greeted by the maitre d', and seated by a window seat. Part of the attraction of Carmel is being able to observe the storybook architecture, and foot traffic, that so exemplifies the atmosphere of this little gem By the Sea. And, yes, this restaurant provides a perfect starting point for that, since it is located right in the middle of all the activities on Ocean Avenue. But, most importantly, it was the delicately prepared cuisine that will assure our return visits to Pangaea Grill. We had a late lunch, so opted for a light Sunset menu dinner for myself, featuring Sand Daps, and Kimchi Fried Rice for Lisa. The Sands Daps were perfectly done and melted in my mouth with a thin buttery crust. I did have a chance to try Lisa's Kimchi Fried Rice. It had the right amount of spice, and herbs, to make it a memorable rice dish. All ingredients, and fragrances of the spices, could be distinctly noted with perfect balance. Frankly, the best version of this dish I ever tasted. Our next visit will assure a more robust appetite and a try at the Korean Short Ribs. We can't wait, and will be back!<//review>

This place is really expensive and not at all worth the payment. I went with a party and we waited half an hour just to order. Our food came out 40 minutes later. I ordered the chicken parmesan and it was extremely flavorless, even the linguini it was placed upon, which is crazy because I paid $26 for it. Everything is pricy and there's no bread, chips, etc. The filet mignon is $38 and it's about the width of a red solo cup and comes with nothing but vegetables. Lobster ravioli had come out cold and was average. The best thing to order is the kimchi stir fry bowl, which is still pricy but the portion makes you feel like you haven't wasted your time and money. At the very end, it was attempted to have one person pay for a group of people under 30 years old as they refused to split the check. A truly terrible experience. The only reason this gets two stars is because the owner is really nice, but definitely out of touch with how the kitchen and its billing procedures are run.< /text>

I want to point out that while I had a great time at the concert, the staffers at Royce Hall did a relatively terrible job managing the show because while a show is going on, it seems that the ushers let people in as the concert in progress. I understand that this is to let people, who paid for their tickets, in but when it gets to the point that so many people are being let in at 20-30 minute intervals and to the point that the performer himself actually has to stop the concert just to let people take their seats, that just completely ruins the experience for everyone. I truly hope that the staff at Royce Hall is made aware of this because if this is a common practice at the performing center, they should know that letting huge groups of people in during the concert just spoils the performance. It is just rude and inconsiderate to the performer and the audience and it would perhaps be ideal to at least let the tardy people come in at the proper timing instead of during a song.</Text>

I saw the Los Angeles ballet perform Swan Lake here. I've seen a lot of great performers at Royce Hall through the years but it didn't work for the ballet that night. The stage was too small and the ballerinas to crammed. Add to that the fact there was no Orchestra but only pre-recorded music and you really should spend a little bit more money to see a Russian ballet in a larger setting. I would have thought it to be okay and worth the money if they had a real Orchestra given they would still look cramped on stage. Unless your idea of a ballet takes place inside of bus bumping around with people the next time they tour like I said spend a little more money and go see the Bolshoi or Kirov.< /Text>
